Resolution No. 557-01.
By Director Konicek.
Be it resolved by the Board of
Control of the City of Cleveland
that, subject to the approval of City

4
Council in accordance with Section
112 of the Charter of the City of
Cleveland, certain new water rates
of the Division of Water for all
direct service customers are hereby
fixed as specified in the following
provisions:
Large Industrial Customers.
All water used in excess of
62,500,000 cubic feet during a three
month
billing
period
shall
be
charged at a rate of seventy-five
percent (75%) of the rate prescribed
in this section for water used in
excess of one thousand (1,000) cubic
feet.
Customers supplied from more
than one service district.
Customers with premises supplied
with water from more than one service district shall be billed at the
rate for the service district from
which the predominant quantity of
water is supplied.
Be it further resolved that Resolution No. 426-00, adopted June 28,
2000, relating to the operation of the
Division of Water, Department of
Public Utilities, is hereby amended
by inserting the foregoing provisions in said resolution under the
headings
“Direct
Service
Water
Rates within Cleveland; Regular
and Special Homestead,” “Direct Service Water Rates in Cuyahoga County Except Cleveland; Regular and
Special Homestead,” and “Direct Service Water Rates in Summit and
Medina Counties; Regular and Special Homestead.”
Be it further resolved that all
other provisions of said Resolution
No. 426-00 not expressly amended
hereby shall remain unchanged and
in full force and effect.
Yeas:
Director
Clark,
Acting
Director Brown, Director Sheperd,
Acting Director DeVaul, Director
Whitlow, Acting Director Smith,
Directors Miller, Hudecek, Acting
Director McCafferty, Director Warren and Acting Director Smith.
Nays: None.
Absent: Director Carr and Acting
Director Badalamenti.
Resolution No. 558-01.
By Director Konicek.
Be it resolved by the Board of
Control of the City of Cleveland that
pursuant to the authority of Ordinance No. 828-2000, passed, by the
Council of the City of Cleveland on
June 12, 2000, Jerome H. Schmelzer
& Associates, is hereby selected
upon the nomination of the Director
of Public Utilities from a list of public relation firms determined, after
a full and complete canvass by said
Director, as the firm to be employed
by contract for the purpose of supplementing the regularly employed
staff of several departments of the
City of Cleveland in order to provide
professional services necessary to
perform research, writing, creative
design, photography, artwork, layout, preparation of camera ready
artwork
and
offset
lithographic
reproduction of the 2000 and 2001
Annual Reports for the Division of
Cleveland Public Power, Department
of Public Utilities.
Be it further resolved that the
Director of Public Utilities hereby is
requested to enter into a written
contract with Jerome H. Schmelzer
& Associates, based upon its proposal dated January 29, 2001, which
contract shall be prepared by the
Director of Law and shall provide
for furnishing of professional services as contained in such proposal

The City Record

August 29, 2001

and shall contain such terms and
conditions as the Director of Law
deems necessary to protect and benefit the public interest.
Be it further resolved that the
work shall commence upon execution of said contract and shall further provide that the aggregate fee
will not be in excess of $90,729.00.
Be it further resolved that the
employment of the following subcontractors to Jerome H. Schmelzer
& Associates, is hereby approved:

described therein and located along
the relocated Old Grayton Road, to

than the fair market value. The

if abandoned by East Ohio Gas.

of Cleveland conveying said easement, which document shall contain
such additional terms and conditions
as are required to protect the interests of the parties.

Whereas, pursuant to Ordinance
No. 2076-76 passed October 25, 1976,
the City is conducting a Land Reutilization Program in accordance with
the provision of Chapter 5722 of the
Ohio Revised Code; and
Whereas, City has acquired Permanent Parcel Nos. 118-18-003, 118-18004, 118-18-005, 118-18-006, 118-18-065,
118-18-067, 118-18-068, 118-18-069, 11818-070, 118-18-071, 118-18-074, 118-18088, 118-18-089, 118-18-090, 118-18-091,
118-18-092, and 118-18-093 under said
Land Reutilization Program; and
Whereas, Ordinance No. 710-01
passed July 18, 2001, authorized the
sale of said parcels for a consideration established by the Board of
Control at not less than the Fair
Market Value; and
Whereas,
Vocational
Guidance
Services has proposed to the City to
purchase and develop said parcels;
now, therefore,
Be it resolved by the Board of
Control of the City of Cleveland that
pursuant to the authorization of
Ordinance No. 710-01 passed July 18,
2001, by the Cleveland City Council,
the Mayor is hereby authorized to
execute an official deed for and on
behalf of the City of Cleveland with
Vocational Guidance Services for
the sale and development of Permanent Parcel Nos. 118-18-003, 118-18004, 118-18-005, 118-18-006, 118-18-065,
118-18-067, 118-18-068, 118-18-069, 11818-070, 118-18-071, 118-18-074, 118-18088, 118-18-089, 118-18-090, 118-18-091,
118-18-092,
and
118-18-093,
as
described in said Ordinance in accordance with the Land Reutilization
Program in such manner as best carries out the intent of said program.
Be it further resolved that the consideration for said parcels shall be
$100 each, which amount is hereby
determined to be not less than the
fair market value of said parcels for
uses in accordance with the Land
Reutilization Program.

CIVIL SERVICE NOTICES
____________

General Information
Application blanks and information, regarding minimum entrance
qualifications, scope of examination,
and suggested reference materials
may be obtained at the office of the
Civil Service Commission, Room 119,
City Hall, East 6th Street, and Lakeside Avenue.
Application blanks must be properly filled out on the official form
prescribed by the Civil Service Commission and filed at the office of the
commission not later than the final
closing date slated in the examination announcement.
EXAMINATION RESULTS: Each
applicant whether passing or failing
will be notified of the results of the
examination as soon as the commission has graded the papers.
Thereafter, eligible lists will be
established which will consist of the
names of those candidates who have
been successful in all parts of the
examination.
PHYSICAL
EXAMINATION:
All
candidates
for
original
entrance
positions who are successful in other
parts of the examinations must submit to a physical examination.
ANNE BLOOMBERG,
President

REPORT OF THE BOARD

CITY OF CLEVELAND
ELECTRIC AGGREGATION
PROGRAM
RULES AND REGULATIONS
The City of Cleveland (“City”) has
created an Electric Aggregation
Program (“Aggregation Program”) to
provide electric generation and related services to customers of The
Cleveland
Electric
Illuminating
Company (“CEI”) who reside in the
City. The City has contracted with
WPS Energy Services, Inc. (“WPS”)
to provide the services for the
Aggregation Program. CEI will continue to provide transmission, distrib ution and ancillary services to customers in the Aggregation Program.
The
following
Rules
and
Regulations have been promulgated
pursuant to Ordinance No. 1960-2000,
passed by the Council of the City of
Cleveland on November 20, 2000.
I. Enrollment
As permitted by state law, the City
created an “opt-out” Aggregation
Program. Under this program, customers are automatically included in
the Aggregation Program. Customers
who wish to participate need not take
any action. Customers who do not
wish to participate must take action
in one of the following three ways:
First, customers may opt-out of the
Aggregation Program by returning
the opt-out postcard enclosed with the
initial notice within ten (10) days.
Second, the customers who did not
return the opt-out postcard are provided another opportunity, called the
Free Switching Period. Notices of the
Free Switching Period are sent to customers once the City and WPS finalize the rates that will be charged to
customers. Customers who receive a
Free Switching Period Notice and do
not wish to participate in the
Aggregation Program will have fourteen (14) days to return an enclosed
post card stating that they do not
want to participate.
Third, customers may opt out by
telephone at any time before the end
of the Free Switching Period by calling the WPS customer service number
at 216-361-1098, or toll-free at 1-800-2772157. All calls are recorded.
Customers who do not opt out by one
of these three methods are automatically enrolled in the Aggregation
Program. There are no charges for
opting out of the program at any time
before the end of the Free Switching
Period. Aggregation Program customers who opt out or switch to another supplier after the Free Switching
Period at the same location shall be
charged a switching fee.
Customers who move into the City
after program start-up, or who are in
the program and move to a different
location within the City, are eligible
to participate in the program at the
Free
Switching
Period
rate.
Customers who choose to join the
Aggregation Program at a later date,
including customers that previously
opted
out
of
the
Aggregation
Program, will be accepted into the
program at either the rate offered
during the Free Switching Period or
at a rate based on market prices.
Customers who opt out of the
Aggregation Program will automati-

cally be provided electric service by
CEI under CEI’s then-current rates.
II. Term of Enrollment
Enrollment in the Aggregation
Program is for a two-year term. Upon
the conclusion of the first term, program customers will receive a notice
stating the rates for the new term and
offering the customers the ability to
opt-out of the program without
charge by returning an enclosed postcard. The opt-out period beginning
with the second term shall be twentyone (21) days in duration.
III. Switching Fees
CEI will charge WPS a $5.00 switching fee for each customer enrolled in
the Aggregation Program. This $5.00
switching fee will be assessed to each
Aggregation Program participant
and will appear on the first month’s
bill. Aggregation Program customers
who switch to another supplier during the first year of the term for service at the same location shall be
charged a $50.00 switching fee.
Customers who switch suppliers during the second year of the term shall
be charged a $25.00 switching fee.
IV. Supplier Switch to WPS
CEI processes a customer’s switch
to an alternate generation supplier
such as WPS at the time of the customer’s monthly meter read. CEI
requires WPS to submit accounts to
be switched twelve (12) business
days prior to the scheduled meter
read
date.
Service
under
the
Aggregation Program commences
after the meter is read.
V. Rates
WPS offers the following electric
generation rates for residential and
commercial customers served by the
Aggregation Program.
Residential
July 2001-May 2002
$.0420/kWh
Residential
June 2002-May 2003
$.0455/kWh
Commercial-CEI Rate 105
May 2001-April 2002
$.0415/KWh
Commercial-CEI Rate 105
May 2002-April 2003
$.0430/KWh
VI. Billin g and Collection Policy
Billing
All customers will continue to
receive a monthly bill from CEI,
which will include charges from WPS
for the electric generation portion of
their bill. Customers are billed according to their CEI bill cycle. CEI bills
customers monthly, in 21 billing
cycles throughout the month.
Payment Terms
Customers are required to pay their
entire CEI bill in a timely manner to
avoid late charges and to maintain
good standing in the program. All
payments are applied to the CEI portion of the bill first. WPS’s charges
will be paid after the amount owed to
CEI is paid in full. Failure to pay the
full amount due, including WPS’s
charges, will lead to termination from
the program. CEI’s billing process
allows residential customers fifteen
(15) days to pay the bill and commercial customers twenty-one (21) days.
At the time of billing, CEI provides
past due notices on accounts thirty
(30) days past due and disconnection
notices to accounts sixty (60) days

2164

August 29, 2001
past due. The CEI notices will include
CEI’s charges to the customer and
will not include WPS’s charges.
Collection Process
Customers are obligated to keep
their accounts current. If WPS does
not receive payment by the bill due
date and an account balance exceeding $25.00 remains past due for thirty
(30) days at the time of billing, a written ten (10) day Past-Due Notice will
be issued. Accounts with a balance
exceeding $25.00 past due sixty (60)
days at the time of billing, and that
were previously issued a Past Due
Notice, will be issued a ten (10) day
written Notification of Intent to
Terminate letter. Accounts remaining
past due after the ten (10) day
Notification of Intent to Terminate
letter will be sent a Program
Termination and Payment Request
Notice. If amounts owed to WPS are
not paid in full within fifteen (15)
days of issuance of the Program
Termination and Payment Request
Notice,
accounts
with
balances
exceeding $25.00 past due will be terminated from the Aggregation Program and returned to CEI. Customers
with accounts returned to CEI for
non-payment are still obligated to pay
WPS the balance owed on the
account.
Customer accounts continuing as
past due after termination from the
Aggregation Program due to nonpayment may be turned over to a collection agency and reported to the credit
bureau, after ten (10) days’ written
notification.
VII. Dispute Resolution
WPS will attempt to resolve all customer complaints in a timely and
good faith manner. Initial response to
the customer’s concern will occur
within five (5) calendar days of complaint.
WPS will investigate customer complaints received from the Public
Utilities Commission of Ohio (PUCO)
and provide a status report to the cus tomer and the PUCO within five (5)
calendar days.
If an investigation into a complaint
received from the customer or a complaint referred by the PUCO is not
completed within fourteen (14) calen dar days, then a status report will be
given to the customer, and, if applicable, the PUCO. These status reports
will be given every five (5) calendar
days until the investigation is complete, unless the action that must be
taken takes longer than five (5) days
and the customer has been notified.
Final results of a Commission referred complaint will be provided to
the PUCO either orally (phone) or in
writing (e-mail, written correspondence), no later than five (5) calendar
days after the investigation is completed. The final results will be provided in writing to the customer no
later than five (5) calendar days after
the investigation is completed.
Customers retain the right to contact the PUCO regarding complaints
and disputes. WPS will provide customers with the current address, telephone numbers, including TDD/TTY
telephone numbers, of the PUCO.
Records of customer complaints will
be retained for one (1) year after the
occurrence of the complaint. A copy of
the complaint record will be provided
to the PUCO within five (5) days, if
requested.
VIII. Warranty Disclaimer, Liability
Except as expressly provided in
these rules and regulations or in the
contracts
between
WPS
and
Aggregation Program participants,

The City Record

August 29, 2001
WPS and the City make no warranties
hereunder,
whether
express
or
implied, including but not limited to
any
implied
warranty
of
merchantability or fitness for a particular purpose.
Except as expressly provided herein, in no event will WPS or the City be
liable for incidental, indirect, special
or consequential damages connected
with or arising from performance or
non-performance of Aggregation Program
services,
irrespective
of
whether such claims are based upon
breach of contract, warranty, tort,
strict liability, or any other legal theory.
IX. Other Terms
Governing Law
Service under the Aggregation
Program shall be governed by the provisions
of
these
Rules
and
Regulations, the City’s Electric
Aggregation
Program
Plan
of
Operation and Governance, the CityWPS Power Supply Agreement, the
Codified Ordinances of the City of
Cleveland, Ohio, 1976, and, to the
extent applicable to WPS, the rules
and regulations of the Public Utilities
Commission of Ohio.
Taxes, Fees
Any taxes, duties, fees or charges
levied against WPS by any governmental or regulatory entity or passed
through to WPS by capacity or energy
shall be passed through by WPS and
paid by the customer. WPS shall provide the customer written notice and
detailed description of such charges
if such information has not been
included in previous communications
or proposals.

Additional Equipment
If additional metering or monitoring equipment is required by CEI,
such metering or monitoring equipment shall be installed at customer’s
expense. Customer shall cooperate as
necessary with installation of additional metering or monitoring equipment.
Customer Information
Neither the City nor WPS shall
release an Aggregation Program participant’s social security number or
account number without the program
participant’s written consent.
Payment History
Aggregation Program customers
shall have the right to request from
WPS the customer’s payment history
for a period of up to twenty-four (24)
months without charge from WPS.
X. Amendment of Rules and Regulations
These Rules and Regulations are
subject to amendment pursuant to the
procedure contained in Ordinance No.
1960-2000, passed by the Council of the
City of Cleveland on November 20,
2000.

ADOPTED RESOLUTIONS
AND ORDINANCES
Res. No. 939-01.
By Councilman Cimperman (by
request).
An emergency resolution declaring
the intention to vacate a portion of
Conn Court N.W.
Whereas, this Council; is satisfied
that there is good cause to vacate a
portion of Conn Court N.W. as hereinafter described; and
Whereas, this resolution constitutes an emergency measure in that
the same provides for the usual
daily
operation
of
a
municipal
department; now, therefore,
Be it resolved by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That it hereby declares
its intention to vacate the following
described real property:
Situated in the City of Cleveland,
County of Cuyahoga and State of
Ohio, and described as being all that
portion of Conn Court N.W. (20.00
feet wide), extending Easterly from
the Westerly line of West 25th
Street (104.00 feet wide) to its Easterly terminus.
Section 2. That this resolution is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and provided it receives the
affirmative vote of two-thirds of all
the members elected to Council, it
shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its adoption and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise, it
shall take effect and be in force from
and after the earliest period allowed
by law.
Adopted August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

Res. No. 1576-01.
By Councilman Brady.
An emergency resolution objecting to the renewal of a C1 and C2
Liquor Permit at 12208 Bellaire Rd.
Whereas, the uniform date for
renewal of liquor permits in the
State of Ohio is October 1st; and
Whereas,
pursuant
to
Section
4303.271 of the Revised Code, the legislative authority of a municipal corporation may object to the renewal
of
a
permit based
upon
legal
grounds as set forth in division (A)
of Revised Code Section 4303.292; and
Whereas, the applicant is unfit to
continue to engage in the liquor permit business in that he has operated his liquor permit business in a
manner that demonstrates a disregard for the laws, regulations or
local ordinances of the state, and
that this objection is based on other
legal
grounds
as
set
forth
in
Revised Code Section 4303.292; and
Whereas, this resolution constitutes an emergency measure provid-

August 29, 2001
ing for the immediate preservation
of the public peace, prosperity, safety and welfare pursuant to Section
4303.271 of the Ohio Revised Code,
objections to renewal of liquor permits shall be made no later than
thirty days prior to the expiration
date of the permit; now, therefore,
Be it resolved by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That Council does hereby record its objection to the renewal of a C1 and C2 Liquor Permit,
Permit No. 0598188, owned by Bellaire Beverage, DBA Bellaire Beverage, 12208 Bellaire Rd., Cleveland,
Ohio 44135 and requests the Director
of Liquor Control to set a hearing
for said application in accordance
with provisions of Section 4303.271
of the Revised Code of Ohio.
Section 2. That the Clerk of Council be and she is hereby directed to
transmit two certified copies of this
resolution, together with two copies
of a letter of objection and two
copies of a letter requesting that the
hearing be held in Cleveland, Cuyahoga County, and a statement by the
Director of Law that, in the Director’s opinion, the objection is based
upon substantial legal grounds within the meaning and intent of division (A) of Section 4303.292 of the
Revised Code to the Director of
Liquor Control.
Section 3. That this resolution is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its adoption and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise, it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Adopted August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

upon substantial legal grounds within the meaning and intent of division (A) of Section 4303.292 of the
Revised Code to the Director of
Liquor Control.
Section 3. That this resolution is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its adoption and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise, it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Adopted August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

Res. No. 1596-01.
By Councilman Coats.
An emergency resolution objecting to the renewal of a C2 and C2X
Liquor Permit at 625 East 140th
Street, 1st Fl.

2172

August 29, 2001
Whereas, the uniform date for
renewal of liquor permits in the
State of Ohio is October 1st; and
Whereas,
pursuant
to
Section
4303.271 of the Revised Code, the
legislative authority of a municipal
corporation may object to the renewal of a permit based upon legal
grounds as set forth in division (A)
of Revised Code Section 4303.292;
and
Whereas, the applicant is unfit to
continue to engage in the liquor permit business in that he has operated his liquor permit business in a
manner that demonstrates a disregard for the laws, regulations or
local ordinances of the state, and
that this objection is based on other
legal
grounds
as
set
forth
in
Revised Code Section 4303.292; and
Whereas, this resolution constitutes an emergency measure providing for the immediate preservation of the public peace, prosperity,
safety and welfare pursuant to Section 4303.271 of the Ohio Revised
Code,
objections
to
renewal
of
liquor permits shall be made no
later than thirty days prior to the
expiration date of the permit; now,
therefore,
Be it resolved by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That Council does hereby record its objection to the renewal of a C2 and C2X Liquor Permit,
Permit No. 6081178, owned by Moes
Stop One Inc., 625 East 140th Street,
1st Fl., Cleveland, Ohio 44110 and
requests the Director of Liquor Control to set a hearing for said application in accordance with provisions
of Section 4303.271 of the Revised
Code of Ohio.
Section 2. That the Clerk of Council be and she is hereby directed to
transmit two certified copies of this
resolution, together with two copies
of a letter of objection and two
copies of a letter requesting that the
hearing be held in Cleveland, Cuyahoga County, and a statement by the
Director of Law that, in the Director’s opinion, the objection is based
upon substantial legal grounds within the meaning and intent of division (A) of Section 4303.292 of the
Revised Code to the Director of
Liquor Control.
Section 3. That this resolution is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of

immediately upon its adoption and

shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.

resolution, together with two copies
of a letter of objection and two
copies of a letter requesting that the
hearing be held in Cleveland, Cuyahoga County, and a statement by the
Director of Law that, in the Director’s opinion, the objection is based
upon substantial legal grounds within the meaning and intent of division (A) of Section 4303.292 of the
Revised Code to the Director of
Liquor Control.
Section 3. That this resolution is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its adoption and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Adopted August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

Res. No. 1620-01.
By Councilman Patmon.
An emergency resolution objecting to the renewal of a C2 and C2X
Liquor Permit at 863-71 East 93rd
Street, 1st Fl.
Whereas, the uniform date for
renewal of liquor permits in the
State of Ohio is October 1st; and
Whereas,
pursuant
to
Section
4303.271 of the Revised Code, the
legislative authority of a municipal
corporation may object to the renewal of a permit based upon legal
grounds as set forth in division (A)
of Revised Code Section 4303.292;
and
Whereas, the applicant is unfit to
continue to engage in the liquor permit business in that he has operated his liquor permit business in a
manner that demonstrates a disregard for the laws, regulations or
local ordinances of the state, and
that this objection is based on other
legal
grounds
as
set
forth
in
Revised Code Section 4303.292; and
Whereas, this resolution constitutes an emergency measure providing for the immediate preservation of the public peace, prosperity,
safety and welfare pursuant to Section 4303.271 of the Ohio Revised
Code,
objections
to
renewal
of
liquor permits shall be made no
later than thirty days prior to the
expiration date of the permit; now,
therefore,
Be it resolved by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That Council does hereby record its objection to the renewal of a C2 and C2X Liquor Permit,
Permit No. 7702571, owned by Samia
Inc., DBA Convenience Deli, 863-71
East 93rd Street, 1st Fl., Cleveland,
Ohio 44108 and requests the Director

2179

25
of Liquor Control to set a hearing
for said application in accordance
with provisions of Section 4303.271
of the Revised Code of Ohio.
Section 2. That the Clerk of Council be and she is hereby directed to
transmit two certified copies of this
resolution, together with two copies
of a letter of objection and two
copies of a letter requesting that the
hearing be held in Cleveland, Cuyahoga County, and a statement by the
Director of Law that, in the Director’s opinion, the objection is based
upon substantial legal grounds within the meaning and intent of division (A) of Section 4303.292 of the
Revised Code to the Director of
Liquor Control.
Section 3. That this resolution is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its adoption and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Adopted August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

grounds as set forth in division (A)
of Revised Code Section 4303.292;
and
Whereas, the applicant is unfit to
continue to engage in the liquor permit business in that he has operated his liquor permit business in a
manner that demonstrates a disregard for the laws, regulations or
local ordinances of the state, and
that this objection is based on other
legal
grounds
as
set
forth
in
Revised Code Section 4303.292; and
Whereas, this resolution constitutes an emergency measure providing for the immediate preservation
of the public peace, prosperity, safety and welfare pursuant to Section
4303.271 of the Ohio Revised Code,
objections to renewal of liquor permits shall be made no later than
thirty days prior to the expiration
date of the permit; now, therefore,
Be it resolved by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That Council does hereby record its objection to the renewal of a D1, D2, D3, D3A and D6
Liquor Permit, Permit No. 1165352,
owned by C & CS Corner Tavern,
DBA
Time
Out
Grill,
17910
Lakeshore Blvd., Cleveland, Ohio
44119 and requests the Director of
Liquor Control to set a hearing for
said application in accordance with
provisions of Section 4303.271 of the
Revised Code of Ohio.
Section 2. That the Clerk of Council be and she is hereby directed to
transmit two certified copies of this

August 29, 2001
resolution, together with two copies
of a letter of objection and two
copies of a letter requesting that the
hearing be held in Cleveland, Cuyahoga County, and a statement by the
Director of Law that, in the Director’s opinion, the objection is based
upon substantial legal grounds within the meaning and intent of division (A) of Section 4303.292 of the
Revised Code to the Director of
Liquor Control.
Section 3. That this resolution is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its adoption and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Adopted August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

the City of Cleveland:

March 5, 2001, and the Clerk of

contract with Brothers Printing Co.
for such services in accordance with
specifications upon which said bid
was received. The cost of said contract shall be payable out of funds
appropriated for Council.

Res. No. 1640-01.
By Councilmen Polensek, Cintron
and Patmon.
An emergency resolution objecting to the closing by Dominion East
Ohio Gas Company of its Payment
and Billing Explanation Center in
Downtown Cleveland, and requesting that the Company reconsider its
decision.
Whereas, Dominion East Ohio Gas
Company has announced the closing
of its last two Payment and Billing
Explanation Centers, including one
located in Downtown Cleveland as
of September 8, 2001, and
Whereas,
72,000
customers
of
Dominion East Ohio Gas Company
depend upon these walk-in Payment
and Billing Explanation Centers,
which provide customers with the
immediate ability to, among other
things, have questions answered,
schedule
investigations
and
rereads, and have gas turned on or
off, and
Whereas, without a walk-in Payment and Billing Explanation Center, customers will be limited to
unreliable call-in centers to have
questions and problems handled,
and such centers often fail to provide proper accessibility and service
to consumers; and
Whereas, for making payments
customers will have to pay up to
$1.00 per transaction to process payments at a store, bank or other business
that
has
contracted
with
Dominion East Ohio to handle such
transactions; and more than a third
of such centers accept cash only;
and
Whereas, the need for personal
contact with representatives of the
gas company has greatly increased
with the advent in October of 2000
of the gas choice program, which
has created confusion and concern
among consumers, and with the
huge increases in rates, causing
many customers to incur delinquencies and require assistance to establish payment arrangements in order
to maintain service; and
Whereas, the closing of Dominion
East Ohio’s Payment and Billing
Explanation Center in Cleveland
would be a blatant attack on consumers in order to save the Company money as it seeks to compete
with gas marketers; and
Whereas, this resolution constitutes an emergency measure for the
immediate preservation of public
peace, property, health or safety,
now, therefore,
Be it resolved by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That the Council of the
City of Cleveland objects to the clos-

August 29, 2001
ing of the Dominion East Ohio Gas
Company
Payment
and
Billing
Explanation Center in Downtown
Cleveland, and urges Dominion East
Ohio to reconsider the closing in
order to adequately serve the needs
of the poor, elderly, and most vulnerable residents of the City of
Cleveland.
Section 2. That the Clerk of Council is hereby directed to transmit
certified copies of this resolution the
Chairman of the Public Utilities
Commission of Ohio and to Dominion East Ohio Gas Company.
Section 3. That this resolution is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its adoption and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Adopted August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001, without
the signature of the Mayor.

this high crime area, which is

outlets, is contrary to the best interests of the entire community; and
Whereas, the applicant does not
qualify to be a permit holder and/or
has demonstrated that he has operated his liquor business in disregard
of the laws, regulations or local
ordinances of this state or any other
state; and
Whereas, the place for which the
permit is sought has not conformed
to the building, safety or health
requirements of the governing body
of this County or City; and
Whereas, the place for which the
permit is sought is so arranged or
constructed that law enforcement
officers or agents of the Department
of Liquor Control are prevented reasonable access to the establishment;
and
Whereas, the place for which the
permit is sought is so located with
respect to the neighborhood that it
substantially interferes with public
decency, sobriety, peace or good
order; and
Whereas, this objection is based
on other legal grounds as set forth
in Revised Code Section 4303.292;
and
Whereas, this resolution constitutes an emergency measure providing for the immediate preservation
of the public peace, prosperity, safety and welfare pursuant to Section
4303.26 of the Ohio Revised Code.
Council’s objection to said permit
must be received by the Director of
Liquor Control within 30 days of
notification; now, therefore,
Be it resolved by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That Council does hereby record its objection to the transfer of ownership of a C1 Liquor Permit from Permit No. 6072057, Mo &
Son Inc., 14510 Kinsman Ave., Cleveland, Ohio 44120 to Permit No.
7682209, Muaad Salem, DBA Kinsman Sunoci, 14510 Kinsman Ave.,
Cleveland, Ohio 44120 and requests
the Director of Liquor Control to set
a hearing for said application in
accordance with provisions of Section 4303.26 of the Revised Code of
Ohio.
Section 2. That the Clerk of Council be and she is hereby directed to
transmit two certified copies of this
resolution, together with two copies
of a letter of objection and two
copies of a letter requesting that the
hearing be held in Cleveland, Cuyahoga County.
Section 3. That this resolution is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,

shall take effect and be in force

allowed by law.

and located at 10004-06 South Boulevard to Famicos Foundation or

has elected to adopt and implement

of the Ohio Revised Code to facilitate reutilization of nonproductive
lands situated within the City of
Cleveland; and

under the City’s Land Reutilization

Community Development under the
terms of Chapter 5722 of the Ohio

Codified Ordinances of the City of
Cleveland, 1976; and
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes an emergency measure providing for the usual daily operation of
a municipal department; now, therefore,
Be it ordained by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:

Commissioner of Purchases and Supplies is hereby authorized to sell
Permanent Parcel No(s). 109-08-127
and
109-08-128,
as
more
fully
described in Section 2 below, to
Famicos Foundation or designee.

to be sold pursuant to Section 1 of
this
Ordinance
is
more
fully
described as follows:
P.P. No. 109-08-127
Situated in the City of Cleveland,
County of Cuyahoga and State of
Ohio, and known as being Sublot No.
125 in the Superior Park Subdivision
No. 2 of part of Original One Hundred
Acre Lots Nos. 376 and 377, as shown
by the recorded plat in Volume 37 of
Maps, Page 5 of Cuyahoga County
Records and being 40 feet front on
the Southerly side of South Boulevard, N.E., and extending back of
equal width 120 feet, as appears by
said plat, be the same more or less,
but subject to all legal highways.
Subject to Zoning Ordinances, if
any.
P.P. No. 109-08-128
Situated in the City of Cleveland,
County of Cuyahoga and State of
Ohio, and known as being Sublot No.
126 in B. Schatzinger’s Superior
Park Subdivision No. 2 of part of
Original One Hundred Acre Lots
Nos. 376 and 377, as shown by the

Page 5 of Cuyahoga County Records
and being 40 feet front on the

N.E., and extending back of equal
width 120 feet, as appears by said
plat, be the same more or less, but
subject to all legal highways.
Subject to Zoning Ordinances, if
any.
Section 3. That all documents necessary to complete the conveyance
authorized by this ordinance shall

of the effective date of this ordinance. If all of the documents are

The City Record
Community Development, this ordinance shall be repealed and shall be

authorized hereby shall be made by

Mayor on behalf of the City of
Cleveland. The deed shall contain
such provisions as may be necessary
to protect and benefit the public
interest.
