Ord. No. 1533-01.
By Councilman Gordon.
An emergency ordinance authorizing and directing the Director of Public Health to enter into a First
Amendment to City Contract No. 50407
with MetroHealth Medical Center.
Whereas, pursuant to Ordinance
No. 93-95, passed March 27, 1995, the
City of Cleveland, through its Director of Public Health, entered into a
Lease By Way of Concession with
MetroHealth Medical Center, Contract No. 50407, for the purposes of
operating outpatient health centers
known as the Thomas McCafferty
Health
Center,
located
at
4242
Lorain
Avenue,
Cleveland,
Ohio,
44113; the Miles-Broadway Health
Center,
located
at
9127
Miles
Avenue, Cleveland, Ohio, 44105; and
the J. Glen Smith Health Center,
located at 11100 St. Clair Avenue,
Cleveland, Ohio, 44108; and
Whereas, the City and MetroHealth began its partnership in
operating the health centers in 1992
and Contract No. 50407 expanded the
role and duties of MetroHealth with
respect to the health centers; and
Whereas, as cited in Contract No.
50407, in entering into the partnership to operate the health centers,
the City and MetroHealth determined that the affiliation would: (i)
better provide for the health and
welfare of the people of the State of
Ohio, the County of Cuyahoga, and
the City of Cleveland, by enhancing
the
availability,
efficiency,
and
economy of Hospital Facilities, as
defined in Section 140.01 of the Ohio
Revised Code, and the services rendered thereby; (ii) provide for cooperation
between
the
City
and
MetroHealth in the utilization of the
shared facilities and services to
obtain economies in operation and
more effective health services; and
(iii) provide efficient operation of
facilities for health services of the
general public without discrimination by reason of race, creed, color
or national origin; and (iv) preserve
and enhance the similar missions
and objectives of the City and
MetroHealth; and
Whereas, the original term of Contract No. 50407 with MetroHealth
expired in June, 2000; however, since
that date, MetroHealth has continued to operate the health centers
and to provide for the medical needs
of the citizens of Cleveland on a
month-to-month basis pending resolution of negotiations concerning a
new lease; and
Whereas, by letter dated June 29,
2001, MetroHealth received a notice
from the Director of Public Health
to vacate the health centers immediately; and
Whereas, this Council is greatly
concerned about assuring that high
quality health care services are
accessible to all citizens of the City
of Cleveland regardless of their
social or economic circumstances; and
Whereas, this Council desires to
ensure that there is no gap in the
provision of health care services for
the residents of our city at the
McCafferty, Miles-Broadway, and J.
Glen Smith health centers; and
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes an emergency measure for the
immediate preservation of public
peace, property, health, and safety;
now, therefore,
Be it ordained by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That notwithstanding
any provisions of the Codified Ordinances of Cleveland, Ohio, 1976 to
the contrary, the Director of Public

The City Record
Health is authorized and directed to
enter into a First Amendment to
Contract No. 50407 with MetroHealth
Medical Center extending the term
thereof until November 30, 2001, with
all other terms and conditions to
remain in effect.
Section 2. That the Director of
Public Health shall work to ensure
that the residents of the City of
Cleveland have uninterrupted access
to primary health care at the health
centers and that the residents of
Cleveland continue to receive quality medical care at the McCafferty,
Miles-Broadway and J. Glen Smith
health facilities.
Section 3. That this ordinance is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its passage and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Passed August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001, without
the signature of the Mayor.

month term commencing September
1, 2001, on the basis of its proposal
dated April 20, 2001, as amended.

any Codified Ordinance of Cleveland, Ohio, 1976, to the contrary, the
Director of Personnel and Human
Resources is hereby authorized to
enter into a contract with Aetna U.S.
Healthcare, Inc. for health maintenance organization-style group health
insurance
coverage
for
City
of
Cleveland employees for a four
month term commencing September
1, 2001, on the basis of its proposal
dated April 20, 2001, as amended.

any Codified Ordinance of Cleveland, Ohio, 1976, to the contrary, the
Director of Personnel and Human
Resources is hereby authorized to
contract with Medical Mutual of
Ohio to provide group dental insurance coverage for eligible City of
Cleveland employees and officers
for a twenty month term commencing September 1, 2001.
Section 8. That the Director of
Personnel and Human Resources is
hereby authorized to contract with
a carrier to provide group vision
insurance for eligible City employees.
The compensation to be paid
for such services shall be set by the
Board of Control.
Section 9. That this ordinance is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,

from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.

Ord. No. 1543-01.
By Councilmen Jackson and Patmon (by departmental request).
An emergency ordinance authorizing the Director of Economic Development to enter into an Enterprise
Zone Agreement with LTV Corporation and/or LTV Steel Company, Inc.
to provide for a ten year abatement
for certain tangible personal property and real estate taxes as an
incentive to expand and improve
their facility at 3100 E. 45th Street,
and for the acquisition of machinery
and equipment located in the Cleveland Area Enterprise Zone.
Whereas, pursuant to Ordinance
No. 948-95, passed June 19, 1995, this
Council designated an area which is
in
the
City
of
Cleveland
and
described in File No. 948-95-A, as the
Cleveland
Area
Enterprise
Zone
(the “Zone”) pursuant to Chapter
5709 of the Ohio Revised Code; and
Whereas, in August, 1995, the
Director of Development of the State
of Ohio determined that the Zone
contains the characteristics set forth
in Section 5709.61(A) of the Revised
Code and certified said area as an
“Urban Jobs and Enterprise Zone”
pursuant to Chapter 5709 of the
Revised Code; and
Whereas, LTV Corporation and/or
LTV
Steel
Company,
Inc.
(the
“Enterprise”) has proposed to LTV
Corporation and/or LTV Steel Company, Inc.; and
Whereas, the Enterprise has certified to the City that, but for abatement of personal property and real
estate taxes the Enterprise would be
at a competitive disadvantage by
operating at this location; and
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes an emergency measure in that
the same provides for the immediate
preservation of the public peace,
safety, property, and welfare and for
the further reason that its enactment
is a necessary prerequisite to providing immediate assistance to create and preserve job opportunities
and advance and promote commercial and economic development in the
City of Cleveland, such assistance
being immediately necessary or such
jobs will be lost; now, therefore,
Be it ordained by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That this Council hereby approves the application of the
Enterprise for enterprise zone incentives on the basis that the Enterprise
is
qualified
by
financial
responsibility and business experience to create and preserve employment opportunities in the Cleveland
Area
Enterprise
Zone
and
to
improve the economic climate of the
City of Cleveland.
Section 2. That the Director of
Economic Development is authorized to enter into an Enterprise
Zone Agreement with the Enterprise
to provide for abatement of certain
tangible personal property and real
estate taxes for a ten year period
beginning in the year such taxes
first become due as an incentive to
LTV Corporation and/or LTV Steel
Company, Inc; said abatement shall
be subject to annual review of the

The City Record
Tax Incentive Review Council.
Section 3. That the terms of said
tax abatement shall be in accordance with the schedule of investments set forth in File No. 1543-01A. The terms of said file notwithstanding, the terms of the tax abatement shall not be amended, nor
shall the tax abatement be assignable or transferrable to any entity,
without the prior legislative authorization by Cleveland City Council.
Section 4. That the Director of
Economic Development is hereby
authorized to charge and accept fees
in an amount not to exceed the maximum allowable under Chapter 5709
of the Revised Code and such funds
are hereby appropriated for the purposes set forth in Chapter 5709 of
the Revised Code. Such fees shall be
deposited to and expended from
Fund No. 17 SF 305, Loan Fees Fund.
Section 5. That the Director of
Law shall prepare and approve said
agreement and that said agreement
shall contain such terms and provisions as he deems necessary to protect the City’s interest.
Section 6. That this ordinance is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its passage and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Passed August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

measure and provided it receives the
affirmative vote of two thirds of all
the members elected to Council, it
shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its passage and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise, it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Passed August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

Ord. No. 1547-01.
By Councilman Lewis.
An emergency ordinance authorizing the sale of real property part of
the Land Reutilization Program and
located on scattered sites to Famicos Foundation Inc., or designee.
Whereas, the City of Cleveland
adopted
and
implemented
procedures under Chapter 5722 of the
Ohio Revised Code to facilitate
reutilization of nonproductive lands
situated within the City of Cleveland; and
Whereas, real property acquired
under the City’s Land Reutilization
Program is acquired, held, administered and disposed of by the City of
Cleveland through its Department of
Community Development under the
terms of Chapter 5722 of the Ohio
Revised Code and Section 183.021 of
Codified Ordinances of the City of
Cleveland, 1976; and
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes an emergency measure providing for the usual daily operation of
a municipal department; now, therefore

the City of Cleveland:

Codified Ordinances of the City of
Cleveland, 1976; and

an emergency measure providing for
the usual daily operation of a municipal department; now, therefore,

granting certain temporary easement
rights to the Board of Commissioners of Cuyahoga County in property
located on Pleasant Valley Road for
a roadway improvement project.

Utilities has requested the sale of
City-owned property no longer needed
for public use and located on Pleasant Valley Road to the Board of Commissioners of Cuyahoga County; and
Whereas, the Board of Commissioners of Cuyahoga County has

Thence South 89° 11' 00" West for
709.00 feet along the centerline of
Pleasant Valley Road to a point;
Thence South 00° 21' 15" East for
40.00 feet to a point, said point being
40.00 feet right of Sta. 114 + 83.20
of Pleasant Valley Road centerline
and the principal place of beginning;
Thence North 89° 11' 00" East for
80.00 feet along the proposed right
of way line to a point on the
Grantor’s Easterly line;
Thence South 00° 21' 15" East for
10.44 feet along the Grantor’s Easterly line to a point;
Thence North 88° 36' 41" West for
20.47 feet to a point;
Thence South 59° 36' 29" West for
50.11 feet to a point;
Thence North 73° 50' 44" West for
16.86 feet to a point on the Grantor’s
Westerly line;
Thence North 00° 21' 15" West for
29.46 feet along the Grantor’s Westerly line to the Point of Beginning.
Description of the above parcel is
based on a survey made by Terin J.
Kaminski, Registered Surveyor No.
7207.
It is understood that the strip of
land above described contains 1,676
square feet (0.038 acres), more or less.
Section 7. That the temporary construction easement shall be nonexclusive and the purpose of the
easement shall be for a roadway
improvement project that includes
pavement widening.
Section 8. That the duration of the
temporary
construction
easement
shall be as long as necessary to
complete the easement may include
reasonable access rights; that the
temporary
construction
easement
shall be assignable; that the temporary construction easement shall
require the grantee to indemnify the
City, provide reasonable insurance,
maintain any grantee improvements
located within the temporary construction easement, and pay any
applicable taxes and assessments.
Section 9. That the temporary construction easement referred to above
shall be made by a temporary rightof-way agreement prepared by the
Director of Law and executed by the
Director of Public Utilities on behalf
of the City of Cleveland. The temporary right-of-way agreement shall
contain such additional terms and
conditions as are required to protect
the interests of the parties. The
Directors of Public Utilities and Law
are authorized to execute such other
documents, including without limitation, contracts for right of entry, as
may be necessary to effect the construction of the road improvements
within the property described in Section 1 of this ordinance.
Section 10. That this ordinance is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives

The City Record
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its passage and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Passed August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

Ord. No. 1551-01.
By Councilmen O’Malley and Patmon (by departmental request).
An emergency ordinance to amend
Sections 535.04, 535.05 and 535.06 of
the Codified Ordinances of Cleveland, Ohio, 1976, as amended by
Ordinance No. 1743-99, passed June
15, 2000, direct service water rates
within Cleveland, regular and special homestead, direct service water
rates in Cuyahoga County except
Cleveland, regular and special homestead and direct service water rates
in Summit and Medina Counties.
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes
an emergency measure providing for
the usual daily operation of a municipal department; now, therefore,
Be it ordained by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That the rates, rules,
and regulations of the Division of
Water, Department of Public Utilities, for water service, fixed by the
Board of Control, be and the same
are hereby approved.
Section 2. That Sections 535.04,
535.05 and 535.06 of the Codified
Ordinances of Cleveland, Ohio, 1976,
as amended by Ordinance No. 174399, passed June 15, 2000, are hereby
amended to read, respectively, as
follows:

(f) Large Industrial Customers.
All water used in excess of 62,500,000
cubic feet during a three month
billing period shall be charged at a
rate of seventy-five percent (75%) of
the rate prescribed in this section
for water used in excess of one thousand (1,000) cubic feet.
(g) Customers supplied from more
than one service district. Customers
with premises supplied with water
from more than one service district
shall be billed at the rate for the service district from which the predominant quantity of water is supplied.

1/1/01 through 12/31/01
A minimum service and consumption charge shall be made to homesteads in Summit and Medina Counties owned by a person sixty-five
years of age or older or a permanently disabled person; provided
that such person obtains a certificate of reduction in taxes pursuant
to the Homestead Exemption provisions of Sections 323.151 through
323.157 of the Revised Code. The
charge for each 1,000 cubic feet of
water used by each homestead shall

homestead during each three month
billing period.

Ord. No. 1552-01.
By Councilman Patmon.
An emergency ordinance authorizing and directing the Director of
Public Service to issue a permit to
the Cleveland Cultural Garden Federation to stretch one banner across
Martin Luther King Jr. Drive north
of Parkgate Ave. on Cleveland Public Power utility poles (by separate
permission) for the period of August
30, 2001 to September 10, 2001, inclusive, to publicize their special annual event; “One World Day”.

78
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes an emergency measure providing for the usual daily operation of
a municipal department; now, therefore
Be it ordained by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That notwithstanding
the provision of Section 623.13 of
the Codified Ordinances of Cleveland, Ohio 1976, the Director of Public Service is hereby authorized and
directed to issue a permit to the
Cleveland Cultural Garden Federation, of Cleveland, Ohio, to install,
maintain and remove one (1) banner to be hung on Cleveland Public
Power utility poles, (by separate
permission) publicizing their special annual event; “One World Day”,
for the period of August 30, 2001 to
September 10, 2001, inclusive, and
which banners are to be hung at
the following pole locations and on
the following pole numbers: Martin
Luther King Jr. Drive - one (1) pole
North of Parkgate Avenue on the
West side of the street, No pole
number or tag; and one (1) pole
North of Parkgate Avenue on the
East side of the street, No pole
number or tag; and which poles
location
and
banners
shall
be
approved by the Director of Public
Service in consultation with the
Director of Public Safety, as to
type, method of affixing and location so as not to interfere with any
sign erected and maintained under
the requirements of law or ordinance. The permission of the owner
of any pole from which banners
will be hung must be obtained prior
to issuance of the permit. No commercial advertising shall be printed or permitted on said banners,
and said banners shall be removed
promptly upon the expiration of
said permit.
Section 2. That this ordinance is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its passage and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Passed August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

Ord. No. 1562-01.
By Councilman Patmon (by departmental request).
An emergency ordinance establishing salary and wage schedules for various classifications, effective as of April
1, 2001, and repealing existing Ordinance No. 434-01, passed March 20, 2000, as amended.
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes an emergency measure providing for the usual daily operation of a municipal
department; now, therefore,
Be it ordained by the Council of the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That this ordinance shall be known as the “General Salary Ordinance.” Further, that except as otherwise herein provided, the schedules of compensation set forth in Sections 2 to 50 inclusive, shall be effective as
of April 1, 2001.
Section 2. Secretary to the Mayor, Directors of Departments, Planning Director, Executive Director Community
Relations Board, four Executive Assistants to the Mayor
(a) That the salary of the Secretary to the Mayor shall be fixed by the Mayor at not less than $49,078.05 and
not more than $154,315.05 per annum.
(b) That the salary of the the Directors of Law, Finance, Public Utilities, Port Control, Economic Development,
Public Safety, Parks, Recreation and Properties, Public Service, Public Health, Personnel and Human Resources,
Community Development, Aging, the Planning Director, and the Executive Director of the Community Relations
Board and four (4) Executive Assistants to the Mayor shall be fixed by the Mayor at not less than $49,078.05 and
not more than $148,750.72 per annum.
Section 3. Clerk of Council
That the salary of the Clerk of Council shall be fixed at not less than $41,416.04 and not more than $93,581.41
per annum.
Section 4. Employees of Council-Salary
That the Clerk of Council, with the approval of the President of Council, shall fix the salary of the employees
of Council within the limits established in the following schedule for each classification:

Ord. No. 1563-01.
By Councilman Polensek.
An emergency ordinance authorizing and directing the Clerk of Council to enter into a contract with
Brothers Printing Company for business cards and note pads for the
Clerk of Council on behalf of the City
Council for a period of two years.
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes an emergency measure providing for the usual daily operation of
a municipal department; now, therefore,
Be it ordained by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That the Clerk of Council be and she hereby is authorized
and directed to make a written
requirement contract in accordance
with the Charter and the Codified
Ordinances of Cleveland, Ohio, 1976,
for business cards and note pads for
a period of two years to be purchased by the Commissioner of Purchases and Supplies upon a unit
basis for the Council of the City of
Cleveland.
Section 2. That the cost of said
contract shall be charged against
the proper appropriation account,
(Fund No. 01 Organization 010101
Account 632000 RL 18136), and the
Director of Finance shall certify
thereon the amount of the initial
purchase thereunder, which purchase, together with all subsequent
purchases, shall be made on order of
the Commissioner of Purchases and
Supplies pursuant to a requisition
against such contract duly certified
by the Director of Finance. Said
requirement contract shall provide
that the contractor shall furnish the
remainder of the Council’s requirements for such goods and/or services, whether more or less than
said estimated quantity, as may be
ordered under subsequent requisitions separately certified against
said contract.
Section 3. That this ordinance is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its passage and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise, it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Passed August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

Ord. No. 1569-01.
By Councilmen Polensek and Cimperman.
An emergency ordinance to supplement the Codified Ordinances of
Cleveland, Ohio, 1976, by enacting
new Section 623.091 thereof, relating
to vandalism of memorials for the
safety forces.
Whereas, this Council recognizes
and honors the tremendous sacrifice
made by police officers and firefighters who have died in the line
of duty while safeguarding the citizens of Cleveland; and
Whereas, this Council believes
that it is fitting that those police
officers, firefighters, and their families should be honored and remembered by the erection and maintenance of memorials; and
Whereas, this Council is appalled
that individuals have chosen to
deface and damage the memorials to
the safety forces through such reckless and thoughtless acts as using
the police officer memorial as recreational equipment for skate boarding, and
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes an emergency measure providing for the usual daily operation of
a municipal department; now, therefore
Be it ordained by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That the Codified Ordinances of Cleveland, Ohio, 1976, are
hereby supplemented by enacting
new Section 623.091 to read as follows:
Section
623.091
Vandalism
to
Police and Firefighter Memorials
(a) No person shall purposely
mar, injure, deface, damage or otherwise
physically
mistreat
the
Police
Memorial
or
Firefighter
Memorial.
(b) Whoever violates this section
is guilty of desecration, a misdemeanor of the second degree.
Section 2. That this ordinance is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its passage and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Passed August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.

Ord. No. 1571-01.
By Councilmen Polensek and Patmon (by departmental request).
An emergency ordinance directing
the Director of Finance to immediately deposit funds from the General Fund into the Neighborhood Equity Fund and the Ward Capital
Improvement Fund.
Whereas, it was Council’s clear
intention
that
the
Neighborhood
Equity Fund and the Ward Capital
Improvement Fund should be fully
funded
and
retain
all
interest
earned by monies deposited into
said funds, and such funds have not
been so funded; and
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes an emergency measure providing for the usual daily operation of
a municipal department; now, therefore
Be it ordained by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That the Director of
Finance is authorized and directed
to immediately deposit from the
General Fund into the Neighborhood Equity Fund, Fund No. 10,
Sub-Fund No. 166, the amount of
Ten Million Five Hundred Thousand Dollars ($10,500,000.00), and
into the Ward Capital Improvement
Fund, Fund No. 10, Sub-Fund No.
168, the amount of Five Million
Five Hundred Seventeen Thousand
Four Hundred Thirty Seven Dollars
($5,517,437.00).
These
respective
amounts are hereby encumbered
within the General Fund for deposit
in said Funds and the purposes of
said Funds.
Section 2. That this ordinance is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its passage and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Passed August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001, without
the signature of the Mayor.

Ord. No. 1573-01.
By Councilman Rybka.
An emergency ordinance authorizing the Director of Community Development to enter into an agreement
with Slavic Village Development Corporation for Architectural Feasibility
Study through the use of Ward 12
Neighborhood Equity Funds.
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes an emergency measure providing for the usual daily operation of
a municipal department; now, therefore
Be it ordained by the Council of
the City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That the Director of
Community Development is authorized to enter into an agreement
with Slavic Village Development
Corporation for Architectural Feasibility Study on the following properties; St. Hyacinth Parish Buildings
at 6114 Franel Street, Our Lady of
Lourdes Convent at 3395 East 53rd
Street, Holy Name School at 8238
Broadway Avenue, and J.L. Goodman Building at 8238 Broadway
Avenue, for the public purpose of
promoting commercial and residential development in the City of
Cleveland, through the use of Ward
12 Neighborhood Equity Funds.
Section 2. That the cost of said
contract shall be in an amount not
to exceed $34,500 and shall be paid
from Fund No. 10 SF 166.
Section 3. That the Director of
Law shall prepare and approve said
contract and that the contract shall
contain such terms and provisions
as he deems necessary to protect the
City’s interest.
Section 4. That this ordinance is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives
the affirmative vote of two-thirds of
all the members elected to Council,
it shall take effect and be in force
immediately upon its passage and
approval by the Mayor; otherwise it
shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Passed August 15, 2001.
Effective August 24, 2001.
